# Dragons of Stormwreck Isle - DM Guide

## 🎲 Quick Reference: Core Mechanics

### Basic Roll Structure

- **d20 + Modifier vs Target Number (DC or AC)**
- Player describes what they want to do → You set DC → They roll
- Higher roll = success

### Th

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive Notion guide for you that covers:

Key Features:

Quick Reference Section - Core mechanics explained simply so you can teach your friends (ability checks, attack rolls, saving throws, crits)
Player Character Tracker - Template for each PC to track their stats, personality, and development outside of Roll20
NPC Reference - All the major characters from Stormwreck Isle with personality notes, voice ideas, and how they connect to plot hooks
Plot Hooks & Side Quests - Both the main adventure hooks and improvised ideas when your players inevitably go off-script
Combat Quick Reference - Turn order, actions, and tips for keeping combat flowing
Session Structure Template - Helps you prep and run sessions smoothly
Session Log Template - Track what happened for continuity
Improvisation Tables - Random NPCs, complications, and names for when you need to think on your feet
DM Tips - Practical advice for new DMs, including common mistakes to avoid

The guide balances your need to over-prepare with the reality that players will surprise you. It gives you solid reference material for teaching mechanics while keeping things accessible and fun-focused.

Pro tip: In Notion, you can duplicate that "Player Character Tracker" section for each of your players, and use the Session Log template after each game. The quick reference sections are perfect for having open on a second screen or phone during play.

Good luck with your first session! Your players are lucky to have such a prepared DM. 🎲

## 📊 Encounter Balancing Cheat Sheet

### Level 1-2 Party (6 Players) ⭐

With 6 players, you need MORE enemies than the module suggests. Use these guidelines:

- **Easy:** 4-6 CR 1/8 creatures OR 2-3 CR 1/4
- **Medium:** 4-6 CR 1/4 creatures OR 2-3 C

# How to Set Up Your D&D Campaign in Notion

## Complete Beginner's Guide (Never Used Notion Before!)

## Step 1: Get Notion (5 minutes)

1. Go to **notion.so**
2. Click **"Try Notion Free"** or **"Sign Up"**

Perfect! I've updated your DM Guide for 6 players and created a complete Notion setup guide for absolute beginners.

What I Changed:

In the DM Guide:

Encounter Balancing - Completely revised for 6 players with specific enemy counts
Specific Stormwreck Isle encounters - Added recommended numbers (e.g., 4-5 zombies instead of 2-3)
Action Economy note - Explains WHY you need more enemies (6 player turns vs enemy turns)
Combat timing - Updated expectations for longer combat with 6 players
Table management tips - Enhanced for managing a larger group

The Notion Setup Guide includes:

Step-by-step account creation (literally never-used-Notion-before level)
How to copy and paste the DM Guide into Notion
How to create pages for all 6 of your players
How to set up session logs
Visual guide showing what your workspace should look like
Keyboard shortcuts and troubleshooting
A week-by-week workflow leading up to your first session
Quick Tips for 6 Players:

Combat will be your biggest challenge. With 6 players, a single combat round takes 6+ turns. To keep it moving:

Set a 30-45 second timer (use your phone)
Have players ready their turn BEFORE it starts
Add enough enemies so it's not "wait 5 turns to do something again"

The good news: 6 players = more chaos, creativity, and memorable moments. Stormwreck Isle is a great starter adventure and can handle the extra players with the adjustments I've added!

Let me know if you have questions about the Notion setup or need any clarifications on the encounter balancing! 🎲

## 👤 User

If I wanted to do ai voice narration for passages - what are some good free / affordable or popular options amongst other DMs?

27 Oct 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

Great question! AI voice narration can really elevate the atmosphere. Here are the most popular options among DMs:

Free Options
ElevenLabs (Most Popular with DMs)
Free Tier: 10,000 characters/month (about 10-15 minutes of audio)
Why DMs love it: Best quality, very natural voices, great for dramatic narration
Best for: Key moments, NPC voices, atmospheric descriptions
Tip: Save your generations as MP3s to reuse without burning credits
Cost if you upgrade: $5/month for 30,000 characters
Google Cloud Text-to-Speech
Free Tier: 1 million characters/month (WAY more than enough)
Why it's good: Completely free for most DM use, decent quality
Best for: Longer passages, letters, journal entries
Setup: Requires a Google Cloud account (free), slightly technical
Voices: "WaveNet" voices sound the best
Microsoft Edge Browser (Built-in)
Completely Free: Unlimited use
How: Edge browser has "Read Aloud" feature (right-click any text)
Why it's underrated: Surprisingly good voices, zero setup
Best for: Quick narration during prep, reading long passages
Tip: Use voices like "Jenny" or "Guy" for natural sound
Affordable Paid Options
ElevenLabs Pro - $5-22/month
Most DMs who pay for something use this
Create custom voices (clone your own or create character voices)
Voice library with fantasy-appropriate options
Sweet spot: $11/month plan (100,000 characters)
Murf.ai - $19/month
Good voice variety
Built-in music/sound effect mixing
Less natural than ElevenLabs but more control
Play.ht - $31/month
Ultra-realistic voices
Good for professional-quality content
Overkill for most DM use
DM Community Favorites (What Actually Gets Used)

Based on r/DMAcademy and DM communities:

1. ElevenLabs Free Tier (60% of DMs who use AI voices)

Save big moments as MP3s
Rotate through different voices for different NPCs
Use sparingly so you don't run out

2. Edge Browser Read Aloud (30%)

Zero cost, always available
Perfect for impromptu "let me read this letter in a cool voice"
Can't save files, but it's instant

3. Google Cloud TTS (10%)

DMs who are tech-savvy
Basically unlimited free use
Can batch-generate all your narration in advance
My Recommendation for You (First-Time DM)

Start with Microsoft Edge "Read Aloud":

Open Edge browser
Copy your narration text
Right-click → "Read aloud"
Choose a voice from the dropdown
It reads it for you!

Why this first: Zero setup, unlimited, you can experiment with different passages to see if your players even like AI narration.

Then try ElevenLabs free tier for your 2-3 most important moments:

The opening scene description
A dramatic letter or prophecy
A key NPC's monologue
Practical DM Workflow
Pre-Session Prep (Week Before)
Identify 2-3 passages you want to narrate dramatically
Generate them with ElevenLabs (save as MP3)
Test audio levels
Have them ready in a folder
During Session
Play the pre-recorded narration at key moments
Use Edge Read Aloud for unexpected situations
Don't overuse it - AI voice works best for special moments
Pro Tips from Experienced DMs

Do:

Use AI narration for handouts, letters, ancient texts
Have a "narrator voice" for scene setting
Mix it with your own voice (you read dialogue, AI reads description)
Test audio levels before the session

Don't:

Use AI for every description (it gets old fast)
Use AI for NPC dialogue if you can do voices (feels less personal)
Let it become a crutch - your own narration is more flexible
Use it for combat descriptions (too slow, breaks flow)
Voices to Try

ElevenLabs free voices:

Adam: Deep, authoritative (great for ominous narration)
Bella: Warm storyteller (general narration)
Antoni: Smooth, mysterious (letters, ancient texts)

Edge Browser voices:

Guy (English UK): Deep, dramatic
Jenny (English US): Clear, friendly narrator
Aria (English US): Warm, storytelling vibe
Quick Setup Guide for ElevenLabs
Go to elevenlabs.io
Sign up (free)
Click "Speech Synthesis"
Paste your text
Choose a voice
Click "Generate"
Download the MP3
Play during your session!
Alternative: Sound Effects Instead

Some DMs find sound effects + music more effective than AI narration:

Free resources:

Tabletop Audio (tabletopaudio.com) - Free ambient tracks
Syrinscape - Free tier available
MyNoise (mynoise.net) - Customizable soundscapes

Honestly, good background music + your own narration often works better than AI voices for maintaining immersion and flexibility.

Would you like me to write out some key narration passages from Stormwreck Isle that would work great with AI voices? I can identify the 3-5 moments where it would have the most impact!

In the dnd world there really isn't the idea of a neutral dragon is there? I would love a illustration of a high fantasy gray dragon behind a dm screen to share with my players

28 Oct 2025

## 🤖 Claude

You're right that D&D traditionally splits dragons into chromatic (evil) and metallic (good), though there are some exceptions like gem dragons (more neutral). A gray dragon works perfectly as a symbolic "neutral arbiter" DM figure!

Let me create that illustration for you:

Gray Dragon Behind DM Screen
Image 
Gray Dragon Behind DM Screen
Image ∙ Version 2 

Perfect! I've created a high fantasy illustration of a majestic gray dragon rising behind a classic DM screen. The dragon has:

Wise, golden eyes with slit pupils (very draconic!)
Neutral gray coloring symbolizing the DM's impartial role
Majestic horns and scales for that epic fantasy feel
A stern but fair expression - the dragon judges impartially
Classic wooden DM screen with a d20 symbol

The "Arbiter of Fate" tagline captures that perfect DM energy - you're not the players' enemy or ally, you're the neutral keeper of the rules and story!

Fun D&D lore note: While traditional chromatic/metallic dragons are good/evil, there ARE some neutral dragons in D&D:

Gem Dragons (amethyst, crystal, emerald, sapphire, topaz) - typically neutral alignments
Moonstone Dragons - chaotic neutral
Some ancient dragons transcend alignment as they age

But a gray dragon as symbolic of the DM's neutral arbitration role? That's perfect! You could even tell your players this dragon represents them - the collective story you're creating together. 🐉

Feel free to download this and share it in your group chat to hype up the campaign!

## 👤 User

My Dragons of Stormwreck isle doesn't come with a player hook for a druid - can we think of the player hook for why a druid might be coming to the cloister on Dragon's Rest? He's a circle of the moon druid so being bear is his thing.

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

Great question! Let me craft a compelling druid hook that ties into Stormwreck Isle's themes and makes a Circle of the Moon druid feel essential to the adventure.

Druid Player Hook Options for Stormwreck Isle
Option 1: The Unnatural Disturbance (Recommended)

The Hook: Your druid has felt a disturbance in the natural balance of the region. The waters around Stormwreck Isle have been sending out "wrong" signals - fish migrating at odd times, seabirds acting erratic, and strange dreams of a bronze dragon calling for help. As a guardian of nature's balance, you've been drawn to investigate Dragon's Rest, a sanctuary known for its harmony between civilization and wilderness.

Why it works:

Ties directly to the undead threat (unnatural creatures disrupting the island)
Makes the druid proactive, not reactive
Bronze dragons are inherently tied to coastal ecosystems
Circle of the Moon = guardian/protector role fits perfectly

Connection to the adventure: The undead rising from the cursed shrine are an affront to nature - creatures that should rest are walking. A druid would absolutely sense this.

Option 2: The Myconid Connection

The Hook: You've received a psychic distress call from the myconids (mushroom folk) in the Seagrow Caves. These peaceful fungal beings have reached out through the natural network of roots and spores, asking for aid. They speak of Dragon's Rest as a place of sanctuary, but something threatens their colony. Your wild shape abilities make you uniquely suited to navigate both the caves and negotiate peace.

Why it works:

Myconids are already in the adventure
Druids often communicate with unusual natural creatures
Direct mission = strong motivation
The stirge conflict gives immediate purpose

Connection to the adventure: This gets your druid immediately involved in one of the main quest hooks and makes them the party's key to befriending the myconids.

Option 3: Runara's Student (Personal Connection)

The Hook: Years ago, you encountered a young bronze dragon wyrmling who was fascinated by your ability to take animal forms. You taught her about the cycles of nature, and she taught you about the balance between civilization and wilderness. She's sent word that Dragon's Rest needs help, and you owe her a debt of friendship. She specifically asked for you because shapeshifting might be needed for reconnaissance.

Why it works:

Creates an immediate bond with the main NPC
Gives the druid special status/relationship
Bronze dragons respect nature and druids
Makes Runara feel more connected to the party

Connection to the adventure: Runara might ask the druid specifically to investigate areas too dangerous for her young form.

Option 4: The Sacred Grove (Mystical)

The Hook: Dragon's Rest was built on the site of an ancient druidic circle. While most have forgotten, your order remembers. The standing stones of the Clifftop Observatory were once used for rituals honoring the wild. You've been sent to check on the site and ensure it hasn't been desecrated. Reports of undead near sacred ground deeply trouble your circle.

Why it works:

Gives the druid ancestral claim to the island
Ties into the Observatory location
Cursed shrine = desecration of sacred space
Historical depth to character motivation

Connection to the adventure: The cursed shrine could be corrupting the old druidic site, making the druid's mission essential.

My Recommendation: Combine #1 and #2

The Complete Hook:

"For weeks, you've felt something wrong in the coastal wilds - a disturbance in the natural order that keeps you awake at night. Then, three nights ago, the dreams began. Not your dreams, but shared visions through the mycelial network that connects all living things. The myconids of Seagrow Caves on Stormwreck Isle are calling for help.

They speak of Dragon's Rest, a sanctuary where a young bronze dragon named Runara tries to maintain balance between civilization and nature. But unnatural forces are rising - creatures that should rest eternally now walk, and the delicate harmony of the island is threatened.

As a Circle of the Moon druid, you are uniquely suited to answer this call. Your wild shape allows you to move between worlds - civilized and wild, land and sea. The myconids need a translator, the island needs a defender, and nature itself is calling you to restore balance.

You've made your way to the docks, preparing to sail to Stormwreck Isle. Whatever darkness threatens the natural order there, you'll face it - whether as elf or as bear."

RP Hooks for the Druid at the Table

Once they arrive, here are some great moments for your druid player:

Arrival Scene:

Runara might comment on sensing "a kindred wild spirit" when meeting the druid
Local wildlife (Sparkpaw the fire gecko, seabirds) are immediately comfortable around them

During the Adventure:

Myconid caves: The druid can naturally communicate/empathize with them
Undead encounters: Strong RP opportunity for revulsion at "unnatural abominations"
Bear form: Swimming to the shipwreck, tracking through the wilderness, intimidating enemies
Clifftop Observatory: Might sense ancient druidic magic in the stones

Character Moments:

Performing rituals to cleanse areas after defeating undead
Teaching other characters about the island's ecosystem
Wild-shaping to scout or speak with animals for information
Bonding with Runara over nature vs. civilization balance

Would you like me to write this up as a formatted handout you can give your druid player? Or add it as a section to your Notion guide?

As a guardian of nature's balance, you've been drawn to investigate Dragon's Rest, a sanctuary known for its harmony between civilization and wilderness.

so here is some back story on my wizard - I want to make a Chronurgy (time) Wizard who's an Astral Elf (might need permission for that) who read from the the Looped Tome and his soul became trapped. Since then he's been reliving his life, stuck in a time loop. He some times doesn't know when things are happening or what is present. He might answer questions really late and if you ever want to do any future telling, my guy might know of things before they happen. He might not change that outcome though because it's something was supposed to happen. He's lived in before.

Lets update the first story to include some fun time references - maybe he's already been there, or maybe he's been there an hundred times and keeps remembering the wrong set of events

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

This is AMAZING character concept! Let me rewrite the wizard's hook with time loop elements that'll be so fun to play:

Wizard Player Hook: The Chronurgy Paradox

The Hook (version for the player):

You've been to Stormwreck Isle before. Or have you? Time has become... unreliable since the Looped Tome.

The memories blur together like watercolors in rain: arriving at Dragon's Rest for the first time (the third time? the hundredth?), meeting Runara the bronze dragon wyrmling who either trusts you immediately or has never seen you before - it depends on which loop you're in. You remember her dying. You remember her thriving. You remember never meeting her at all.

What you DO know - what echoes across every iteration - is that something is deeply wrong with time on Stormwreck Isle. The undead rising from the cursed shrine aren't just an affront to life; they're an affront to linear causality. Creatures that should be past-tense are present-tense. Time is wounded there, bleeding into itself.

Maybe that's why you keep being drawn back. Or maybe you never left. Perhaps this is the loop where you finally fix it. Or perhaps you've already fixed it and this is the echo.

In your most recent vision (dream? memory? premonition?), you saw the party you'd travel with. You've seen them before - you think. The druid who speaks of balance. The others whose faces shift between loops. This time, you'll try something different. Or maybe you've said that before.

You stand at the docks, ticket in hand (did you buy it yesterday or ten years ago?), preparing to return to Stormwreck Isle for the first time. Again.

The Looped Tome's curse means you're uniquely suited to solve temporal anomalies. You just hope you remember this conversation when it becomes relevant. You probably won't. You never do.

But maybe this loop is different. They always are. They never are.

DM Notes for Playing the Time Loop Wizard
Core Concept

This wizard exists slightly outside normal time. He's experienced multiple versions of events, so his responses and knowledge are unpredictable.

How to Play This at the Table

Answering Questions Late:

Someone asks "What's your name?" in Session 1
Wizard answers in Session 3 randomly: "Oh, you asked my name two weeks ago. Sorry, time got away from me."

Prophetic Knowledge:

DM: "You enter the cave and see—"
Wizard: "Three zombies and a trapped door on the left. Yes, I remember now. Or... will remember? Let's proceed carefully."
(Give him vague correct information sometimes, wrong information other times - he's remembering different loops)

Temporal Confusion:

"Wait, haven't we killed this kobold already? No? We will then. Are going to. Did?"
"Oh good, you're all alive! Last time we— nevermind, this is the first time. Forget I said anything."

Meeting NPCs:

Meeting Runara: "Runara! Good to see you again. Wait... no, this is... squints ...the first time? You look younger. Or I look older. When are we?"
Runara: "Um... have we met?"
Wizard: "Not yet. I mean, yes. I mean... let's start over."
Mechanical Hooks for You as DM

Give him false memories:

"You remember Myla warning you about the underwater entrance. Except she hasn't done that yet. Or maybe she won't in this loop."

Let him "remember" things:

Perception check at a door: "Oh, I remember this one. Trapped? No wait, that's next door. Or was it the chest? Time is difficult."

Prophetic but useless warnings:

"Someone's going to get injured in the next fight. Badly. I can't remember who. I think it was... everyone? Be careful."

Perfect dramatic moments:

BBEG monologue: "Yes, yes, you want to plunge the world into darkness. You've told me this before. Can we skip to the fight? I remember this speech being quite long."
Fun RP Moments

Early in Adventure:

"I'm glad we're all getting along. We make a good team. We're going to make a good team. Grammar is hard when you're temporally unmoored."

Mid-Adventure:

Picks up a magic item "Oh! I've been looking for this. I lost it next week."

Meeting someone for the "first" time:

"Derek! How's your sister?"
"My name's not Derek and I don't have a sister."
"...Different loop. My apologies, [squints at them trying to remember]... Tim?"

During combat:

"Duck!" fireball flies overhead
"How did you know?!"
"You told me about it later. Will tell me. The grammar for time travel is impossible."
Connecting to the Stormwreck Isle Plot

The Cursed Shrine connection: The undead are rising because time is broken there. The shrine doesn't just raise the dead - it's pulling creatures from different time periods. The wizard recognizes this because he experiences something similar.

Possible revelation mid-adventure: "Wait... I think the curse on that shrine and the curse on me are related. The Looped Tome wasn't just any artifact - it was created HERE. Or will be created. Or... we need to destroy it before it's made? After? Causality is giving me a headache."

The "fix" might break his loop: If they cleanse the shrine, maybe it weakens his curse too. Or strengthens it. He's not sure which. He's lived both outcomes.

Or... dark twist: "I've done this a hundred times. We always win. But then I wake up at the docks again. What if... what if YOU'RE all in MY loop? What if we're trapped here together until we do something differently?"

Quotes to Use
"Is this your first time meeting me, or mine?"
"I'd offer you advice, but I can't remember if it's helpful or if I'm thinking of a different timeline."
"Don't worry, I've died here before. It's not pleasant, but it's temporary. Everything is."
"The thing about living in loops is you stop fearing death and start fearing repetition."
"I brought healing potions! ...I think. Or maybe I'll bring them tomorrow-yesterday."
Permission for Astral Elf Chronurgy Wizard

This is from Explorer's Guide to Wildemount (Chronurgy) and Spelljammer/Mordenkainen Presents: Monsters of the Multiverse (Astral Elf). Both are official D&D content.

As the DM, I'd absolutely allow this because:

The backstory is incredible and adds depth
Astral Elves have ties to Wildspace/time-space weirdness (fits perfectly)
Chronurgy wizards are balanced mechanically
The RP potential is chef's kiss
It gives you as DM SO many fun narrative tools

Would you like me to add this to your Notion guide as a player handout section? I can also create some "Time Loop Wizard Moments" reference cards for you to slip into gameplay randomly!

## 👤 User

If you make a variant human, are you restritcted to a certain list of feats or is it any feat in dnd 5e?

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

Great question!

Variant Human can choose ANY feat available in D&D 5e - there's no restricted list. The only requirement is that you meet any prerequisites the feat has (which most level 1 feats don't have).

What Variant Human Gets:
+1 to TWO different ability scores (your choice)
Proficiency in ONE skill of your choice
ONE feat of your choice
Common Prerequisites to Watch For:

Most feats have NO prerequisites, but a few do:

Feats with ability score requirements:

Heavily Armored - Need Str 13 and proficiency with medium armor
Medium Armor Master - Need proficiency with medium armor
Heavy Armor Master - Need proficiency with heavy armor

Feats with class/proficiency requirements:

Martial Adept - No requirements (anyone can take it)
Spell Sniper - Need ability to cast at least one spell
War Caster - Need ability to cast at least one spell

Feats with other feats as requirements:

Heavily Armored - Need Medium Armor proficiency
Popular Level 1 Variant Human Feats:

For your group, depending on classes:

Lucky - Reroll 3 d20s per day (universally amazing)
Alert - +5 initiative, can't be surprised (great for new players)
Magic Initiate - Learn 2 cantrips + 1 1st-level spell from another class
War Caster - Advantage on concentration saves (amazing for casters)
Resilient - +1 to an ability score and proficiency in that save
Tough - Extra HP (great for frontliners)
Crossbow Expert - Ignore loading, no disadvantage at close range
Sharpshooter - -5 to hit, +10 damage (powerful but risky at level 1)
Why This Matters for Your Time Wizard:

If your player is worried about being "too complicated" with Astral Elf + Chronurgy, Variant Human is actually perfect for a time wizard too!

They could take:

Lucky feat (fits perfectly - "I remember this roll going differently")
Alert (time wizard sees things coming)
Keen Mind (perfect memory across timelines)

The flavor would work just as well, and Variant Human is in the basic Player's Handbook so no permission needed!

Bottom Line: Variant Human = any feat you want (as long as you meet prerequisites, which are rare at level 1). It's one of the most flexible and powerful race choices for exactly this reason!

Is your wizard player considering Variant Human instead of Astral Elf, or is someone else in the party thinking about it?

## 👤 User

This would be for a new druid character a player is playing - moon druid I believe

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

Perfect! A Variant Human Circle of the Moon Druid is actually a really strong choice, and getting a feat at level 1 can give them some great options.

Best Feats for a Level 1 Moon Druid
Top Tier Choices:

1. War Caster (My #1 Recommendation)

Why it's perfect: Moon druids are on the frontlines in wild shape, and you'll be maintaining concentration spells (like Entangle or Faerie Fire) while getting hit
What it does:
Advantage on concentration saves
Can perform somatic components with hands full (shield + weapon)
Can cast spells as opportunity attacks (less useful early)
Why for Moon Druid: You'll be a bear getting smacked, trying to keep Entangle up. This is HUGE.

2. Resilient (Constitution)

Why it's good: +1 CON and proficiency in CON saves
What it does: Makes concentration saves much more reliable
Why for Moon Druid: Your wild shape forms use YOUR CON save proficiency, so this protects concentration in bear form
Note: Choose this if you have an odd CON score (like 15) to round it up to 16

3. Lucky

Why it's great: 3 rerolls per long rest on ANY d20 roll
What it does: Save a failed wild shape attack, reroll a bad save, force enemy to reroll a crit
Why for Moon Druid: Universal safety net, great for new players
Flavor: "Nature guides my instincts" or "The bear spirit warned me"

4. Tough

Why it's solid: +2 HP per level (so +2 HP at level 1, +4 at level 2, etc.)
What it does: More survivability
Why for Moon Druid: Your wild shapes are separate HP pools, so this only affects your caster form, BUT it keeps you alive when you get knocked out of wild shape
Note: Less optimal than War Caster, but simpler for new players
Good But Less Optimal:

5. Alert

+5 initiative, can't be surprised
Good for getting into bear form before enemies act
Less critical than concentration protection

6. Observant

+5 passive Perception and Investigation, +1 WIS
Great for exploration/RP
Doesn't help in combat much

7. Magic Initiate

Get 2 cantrips + 1 1st-level spell from another class
Less useful since druids already have great spells
Could grab Cure Wounds if going non-druid class, but redundant
What I'd Recommend:

For a NEW player playing Moon Druid: War Caster or Lucky

Why War Caster:

Moon druids are concentration-heavy
You'll be in wild shape (bear form) on the frontlines getting hit
Advantage on concentration saves = your Entangle stays up = party wins fights
Simple to understand: "I get advantage when hit while concentrating"

Why Lucky (alternative):

More forgiving for new players
"I can fix mistakes 3 times per day"
Works in ANY situation
Easier to remember and use
Ability Score Setup Suggestion:

With Variant Human for a Moon Druid:

+1 WIS, +1 CON (most common)
Feat: War Caster or Lucky
Skill proficiency: Perception (or something flavorful)

Example stat array (standard array):

STR 13, DEX 12, CON 14, INT 8, WIS 16 (+1), CHA 10
With Variant Human: WIS 16, CON 15 → both become 16, 15
Take War Caster
Your concentration saves are solid!
Wild Shape + Feat Synergy:

Important: When you wild shape:

You keep your proficiencies (including feat benefits)
You use the beast's physical stats (STR, DEX, CON)
You use YOUR mental stats (INT, WIS, CHA)
War Caster advantage applies to YOUR concentration saves (using the beast's CON modifier + your proficiency)

So War Caster works PERFECTLY with wild shape!

Updated Player Hook with Variant Human Flavor:

Since we had that nature disturbance hook, here's how it works as a Variant Human:

"You've always been more attuned to nature than most humans. Where others see coincidence, you see patterns. Where others see animals, you see kin. [If War Caster: Your connection to the wild gives you unshakeable focus - when the bear spirit fills you, nothing can break your concentration.]

For weeks, you've felt something wrong in the coastal wilds..."

(Rest of hook stays the same!)

Does your player know they want Moon Druid, or are they still deciding? Moon Druid is EXCELLENT for new players - very forgiving, straightforward combat (turn into bear, bite things), and super fun!

## 👤 User

Can a level 1 druid take warcaster if they only access to cantrips?

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

Yes, absolutely! A level 1 druid can take War Caster.

War Caster Prerequisites:

The feat requires: "The ability to cast at least one spell"

Cantrips count as spells! So as long as your druid has access to cantrips (which all druids do from level 1), they meet the requirement.

What Level 1 Druids Have:
2 cantrips (like Shillelagh, Produce Flame, Guidance)
Spell slots for 1st-level spells (Entangle, Cure Wounds, Goodberry, etc.)

So they definitely qualify!

War Caster Benefits for Level 1 Druid:
Advantage on concentration saves ✓ (Works immediately with spells like Entangle, Faerie Fire, Thunderwave)
Somatic components with hands full ✓ (Can hold shield + club and still cast)
Cast spells as opportunity attacks ✓ (Works with cantrips like Produce Flame, though situational at level 1)
The Opportunity Attack Feature:

The third benefit (casting spells as opportunity attacks) actually becomes REALLY cool when they wild shape:

Normally in wild shape, you can't cast spells
BUT if you have War Caster, when you drop out of wild shape and an enemy is in melee range, you can immediately reaction-cast a spell as they try to escape
At higher levels this is clutch!

TL;DR: Yes, cantrips count! War Caster is 100% legal and excellent for a level 1 druid, especially a Moon Druid who'll be concentrating while tanking in bear form.

Any other character creation questions for your 6-player crew?

## 👤 User

what is the challenge level 1 wild shape options available to a level 2 circle of the moon druid

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

Great question! Circle of the Moon druids get MUCH better wild shape options than other druids.

Circle of the Moon Level 2 Wild Shape Rules:
CR limit: CR 1 (instead of CR 1/4 for other druids)
Movement: Can have swimming speed
No flying speed (not until level 8)
CR 1 Beast Options Available:
Top Tier (The Good Stuff):

1. Brown Bear ⭐ (The Classic)

HP: 34
AC: 11
Speed: 40 ft., climb 30 ft.
Attacks:
Bite: +5 to hit, 1d8+4 piercing
Claws: +5 to hit, 2d6+4 slashing
Why it's amazing: Highest HP pool at this level, great damage, good mobility
Best for: Frontline tanking, being an absolute unit

2. Dire Wolf ⭐

HP: 37 (HIGHEST!)
AC: 14 (HIGHEST!)
Speed: 50 ft.
Attacks: Bite: +5 to hit, 2d6+3 piercing
Special: Pack Tactics (advantage on attacks if ally is within 5 ft. of target)
Why it's amazing: Best AC and HP combo, Pack Tactics is INCREDIBLE with a party of 6
Best for: Team-based combat, hit-and-run tactics

3. Giant Hyena

HP: 45 (TECHNICALLY HIGHEST but see note below)
AC: 12
Speed: 50 ft.
Attacks: Bite: +5 to hit, 2d6+3 piercing
Special: Rampage (bonus action bite attack when you reduce enemy to 0 HP)
Why it's good: Most HP, can get extra attacks
Best for: Mowing through multiple weak enemies
Note: Some DMs don't allow this because it's from Curse of Strahd and meant to be setting-specific

4. Giant Toad

HP: 39
AC: 11
Speed: 20 ft., swim 40 ft.
Attacks: Bite: +4 to hit, 1d10+2 piercing plus grapple
Special: Swallow (if you grapple a Small creature and hit again, you swallow them - they take acid damage)
Why it's situational: Grapple + swallow is hilarious and effective against small enemies
Best for: Underwater encounters, controlling single targets
Solid Options:

5. Giant Eagle

HP: 26
AC: 13
Speed: 10 ft., fly 80 ft.
Wait... flying? Some DMs allow this since it's CR 1, but RAW says "no flying speed until level 8"
Check with your DM! If allowed, it's incredible for scouting/mobility

6. Tiger

HP: 37
AC: 12
Speed: 40 ft.
Attacks: Bite +5 (1d10+3), Claws +5 (1d8+3)
Special: Pounce (if you move 20+ ft. straight and hit with claws, target makes DC 13 STR save or gets knocked prone, giving you a bonus bite attack)
Why it's good: High damage output if you can set up Pounce
Best for: Ambush tactics, burst damage

7. Lion

HP: 26
AC: 12
Speed: 50 ft.
Attacks: Bite +5 (1d8+3), Claws +5 (1d6+3)
Special: Pounce (same as tiger), Pack Tactics, Running Leap (can long jump 25 ft. with 10 ft. run-up)
Why it's good: Like tiger but with Pack Tactics
Best for: Party coordination
Niche/Situational:

8. Giant Spider

HP: 26
AC: 14
Speed: 30 ft., climb 30 ft.
Special: Spider Climb, Web Sense, Web Walker, can blind enemies with webs
Best for: Climbing, stealth, battlefield control

9. Giant Octopus

HP: 52 (INSANE!)
AC: 11
Speed: 10 ft., swim 60 ft.
Special: Hold Breath (1 hour), underwater camouflage, tentacle attacks with grapple, ink cloud
Best for: Underwater combat ONLY (10 ft. land speed is crippling)
Why it's weird: Amazing stats but you're almost immobile on land

10. Giant Vulture

HP: 22
AC: 10
Speed: 10 ft., fly 60 ft.
Special: Pack Tactics, Keen Sight and Smell
Same flying caveat as Giant Eagle
My Recommendations for Stormwreck Isle:
Primary Form: Dire Wolf
Best AC/HP combo
Pack Tactics with your 6-person party = almost always have advantage
Fast movement for positioning
Island has lots of outdoor encounters
Secondary Form: Brown Bear
Slightly tankier feeling (lower AC but similar HP)
More damage on claws
Classic "I'm a bear" energy
Climbing speed is useful
Situational Form: Giant Toad
Stormwreck Isle has water encounters (shipwreck, caves with pools)
Swim speed is clutch
Grappling small enemies is fun
Combat Math for Your Player:

Dire Wolf with Pack Tactics (with 5 other party members around):

Attack roll: +5 to hit with advantage (almost always someone near your target)
Damage: 2d6+3 (avg 10) piercing
You can take 34 damage before being knocked back to elf form
At level 2, you can wild shape twice per short rest
That's potentially 68 extra HP in a single combat!

For comparison, a level 2 druid probably has:

12-16 HP normally
So wild shape gives you 3-4x your normal HP pool
Quick Reference Card for Your Player:

HP: 37 | AC: 14 | Speed: 50 ft.
Bite: +5, 2d6+3 damage
★ Pack Tactics = Advantage!

HP: 34 | AC: 11 | Speed: 40 ft.

Claws: +5, 2d6+4 damage
Climb: 30 ft.

HP: 39 | AC: 11 | Speed: 20/swim 40
Bite: +4, 1d10+2 + grapple
★ Can swallow Small creatures!

Does your druid player know about the bonus action wild shape that Moon druids get? That's HUGE - they can wild shape as a bonus action instead of a full action, meaning they can cast a concentration spell (like Entangle) and THEN turn into a bear in the same turn!

## 👤 User

Ok! New character information - here is my druid's back story - and from this I want to update his player hook as to why he's coming to dragon rest

Trenzor, Human Druid of the Tall Trees
Background: Folk Hero (Cartographer’s Son) Homeland: Waterdeep → The High Forest (Tall Trees Grove) The Mapmaker’s Son
Trenzor was born in the bustling city of Waterdeep, the only child of a family of respected cartographers. His parents, Mara and Halden Varro, were renowned for charting the ever-shifting frontiers of Faerûn. They believed maps were more than ink on parchment—they were stories of the world itself, living and changing like nature. Trenzor grew up amid scrolls, compasses, and tales of distant horizons.
When Trenzor was barely ten, the Varro family joined a caravan to chart a safer trade route near the High Forest. That journey would be their last together. Gnolls, driven by a hunger beyond reason, ambushed their caravan. Trenzor’s parents were slain defending their work, their maps burning in the chaos. The boy fled into the forest, wounded and alone.
Child of the Tall Trees
For days, Trenzor wandered the vast wilderness until he was found by the Druids of the Tall Trees, protectors of the ancient High Forest. They saw in him something rare—a human child who looked upon nature not with fear, but reverence. The druids took him in, teaching him their ways: the balance of life and decay, the language of beasts, and the art of shaping the world’s primal energy.
As he grew, Trenzor’s curiosity never faded. He drew maps of root networks, rivers, and ley lines, blending his parents’ craft with the druids’ wisdom. He became a folk hero among the grove’s younger initiates—known for defending travelers from monsters, restoring burnt groves, and even confronting poachers who sought to defile sacred lands.
But as time passed, the call of exploration stirred again. Trenzor began to dream of his parents’ lost maps—visions of coastlines and islands marked by strange sigils. He took it as a sign: his journey wasn’t finished. It was only beginning.
Journey to Stormwreck Isle
Setting out with a druid’s staff and his parents’ compass, Trenzor boarded a merchant vessel bound for distant waters. Yet fate had one more twist in store. A storm—unnatural and fierce—drove his ship onto the shores of Stormwreck Isle.
There, he senses something amiss. The land whispers of corruption beneath its beauty. The balance is shifting, and the island hides secrets that could rewrite what Trenzor thought he knew about nature, magic, and perhaps even the fate of his family’s work.

11 Nov 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

This is a FANTASTIC backstory! The cartographer connection, the tragic loss, the folk hero angle, and the connection to his parents' lost maps all give us so much to work with. Let me rewrite his player hook to weave all of this together:

Trenzor's Player Hook: The Map That Called Him Home

The Hook:

The compass has been acting strangely for weeks.

Your parents' compass—the only thing you saved from the gnoll attack all those years ago—has always pointed true north. Until now. Three weeks ago, it began to drift, pulling subtly toward the coast. At first, you thought it broken. Then you realized: it wasn't pointing north anymore. It was pointing somewhere.

The dreams came next. Not the usual visions of root and stone that guide a druid's sleep, but fragments of your parents' final maps. Coastlines you'd never seen. An island marked with a symbol you half-remember from childhood—a bronze dragon coiled around a tower. And always, your mother's voice: "Some places call to be mapped, Trenzor. They have stories that need telling."

You consulted the eldest druids of the Tall Trees. They recognized the signs: a disturbance in the natural order, far to the east where land meets sea. The balance is shifting. Something unnatural stirs—creatures that should rest walk again, and the boundary between life and death grows thin.

But there's something more. In the grove's ancient library, you found a fragment—a charred corner of one of your parents' maps, preserved by the druids who found you. On it, barely legible: "Stormwreck Isle - Dragon's Rest - Sanctuary of Balance."

Your parents had been there. Or were meant to go there. The compass knew.

So you did what any son of cartographers would do: you followed the map. You booked passage on a merchant vessel bound for the eastern waters, compass in hand, ready to finish what your parents started.

The storm that drove your ship onto Stormwreck Isle's shores was violent and sudden—unnatural in its fury. As you dragged yourself from the wreckage onto the beach, the compass finally went still. You'd arrived.

Standing on the sand, staff in hand, you feel it immediately: the island is sick. The trees whisper of corruption. The balance your druid mentors taught you to protect is wounded here, bleeding into itself. Undead walk where they should rest. Time and nature are at war.

But beneath the wrongness, you sense something else—sanctuary. Dragon's Rest. A place where druids and dragons once worked together to preserve harmony between civilization and wilderness. If the balance can be restored anywhere, it's here.

Your parents' map led you here for a reason. Perhaps it's to finish their work. Perhaps it's to save this place. Perhaps it's simply because some stories need a mapmaker to tell them.

The compass points inland now, toward the heart of the island. Toward Dragon's Rest. Toward whatever called you home.

DM Notes: Weaving Trenzor into Stormwreck Isle
Connection to the Main Plot

The Cursed Shrine: The undead rising from the shrine represent exactly what Trenzor was trained to fight—an imbalance between life and death, nature corrupted by unnatural magic. This is his purpose as a Tall Trees druid.

His Parents' Map: Here's a beautiful twist you can use: What if Trenzor's parents were mapping Dragon's Rest because they'd heard rumors of a place where different peoples (dragons, elves, dwarves, humans) lived in balance with nature? They wanted to document it as proof that such harmony was possible. They never made it there, but their son did.

The Compass: The compass can be a plot device throughout the adventure:

It points toward sources of imbalance (the cursed shrine, undead concentrations)
Runara might recognize it: "A cartographer's compass... attuned to ley lines. Your parents were wise."
Late in the adventure, it might reveal something hidden on the island
Key RP Moments for Trenzor

Meeting Runara:

She might say: "Your parents... I've heard of them. The Tall Trees druids speak of cartographers who sought to map the bonds between civilizations. I'm sorry they never reached us."
This creates an instant bond—Runara represents what his parents were seeking

At the Clifftop Observatory:

Ancient stone circle with astronomical markings
Trenzor recognizes it as a mapping site—his parents would have loved this
Maybe he finds weathered cartographer's tools here, left by previous mapmakers
Opportunity for a touching moment: "They were here. Or meant to be."

In the Myconid Caves:

The myconids communicate through spores and shared visions
They might share a memory of "humans with mapping tools" who passed nearby years ago
"They smelled of ink and parchment and hope. The forest mourned when they fell."

Facing the Undead:

Each victory restoring balance is personal
"You took my parents. You won't take this island."
Folk hero moment: protecting others from the same fate

Mapping the Island:

Throughout the adventure, Trenzor can sketch maps as his parents would have
By the end, he completes their map of Stormwreck Isle
Perhaps he sends it back to the Tall Trees grove, or gives it to Runara as a gift
Tying It to Other Characters

The Time Wizard: If you have the time-loop wizard, there's potential for: "I've seen your parents. In another loop. They made it here, once. It... didn't end well. But maybe this time is different."

The Party: Trenzor is a folk hero—he naturally becomes the protector of the group. He's seen loss, knows what it means to be saved, and will do everything to prevent others from suffering his fate.

The Compass as a Story Device

Session 1-2: Points vaguely toward Dragon's Rest, then toward the cursed shrine area

Mid-Adventure: Starts spinning wildly near sources of corruption, helps the party locate undead concentrations

Climax: When they cleanse the shrine, the compass goes still—balance is restored. Or... it points toward something else. A bigger imbalance elsewhere. Adventure hook for later!

Epilogue: Trenzor can choose to stay at Dragon's Rest (continuing his parents' dream of documenting harmony) or continue exploring (following the compass to wherever balance needs restoring)

Updated Quick Reference for Trenzor

Personality Traits:

Curious cartographer—always sketching, documenting, observing
Folk hero protector—will not let others suffer as he did
Carries grief quietly but purposefully

Ideals:

Balance must be preserved (druid teaching)
Stories deserve to be told (parents' legacy)
Civilization and nature can coexist (what his parents sought)

Bonds:

The Tall Trees druids who raised him
His parents' memory and unfinished maps
The compass—his last connection to them

Flaws:

Sometimes too focused on documenting instead of living in the moment
Feels responsible for "finishing" things others started
Protective to the point of self-sacrifice

Key Item:

Parents' Compass - ornate brass compass, slightly scorched, points toward "imbalance" rather than north
Opening Scene Suggestion

When Trenzor washes ashore after the shipwreck, you could describe:

"Salt water burns your lungs as you drag yourself onto the beach. The storm has passed as suddenly as it came—too sudden, too violent, too wrong. Your druid senses scream that this was no natural weather.

In your hand, somehow still clutched tight, is your father's compass. The glass is cracked but unbroken. And for the first time in weeks, the needle has stopped its restless wandering. It points steadily inland, toward a hill where you can just make out stone buildings nestled among ancient trees.

Dragon's Rest. You made it.

The sand beneath your fingers is wrong—too cold, too still. You press your palm flat and reach out with your druid senses. The island whispers back: corruption, imbalance, death where there should be life.

But also: sanctuary. Hope. A bronze dragon who still believes in the dream your parents died for.

You stand, waterlogged but unbroken, and follow the compass toward your destiny."

This gives Trenzor a deeply personal connection to the island while making him the perfect character to restore balance. His parents' dream lives on through him, and completing their map becomes completing their mission.

Want me to add this to your Notion guide as a player handout?

- **Hard:** 1 CR 1 + 2 CR

Memorable and unique

Running the Circus Owlbear:

If they feed it and succeed on Animal Handling:

It follows them for this travel segment
In combat, it can make one attack per round (your control)
It does the "Dance!" trick when they rest (adorable moment)
At the next location, it wanders off into the woods (or they can try to keep it at Dragon's Rest)

If they fight it:

Standard owlbear combat (CR 3, so this is HARD for level 1-2 party)
Tone it down: Give it 40 HP instead of 59
It tries to flee if reduced below 15 HP

Cargo from the shipwreck (circus was traveling by sea)
Previous adventurers who died on the island
A traveling carnival that visited Dragon's Rest years ago

I like would so help - in my discord channel I want to create a session timeline recap that I would love assistance writing... Session 1 -
Our Adventures Trenzor(Druid), Harlen Vex(Fighter),Levendel 'Levy' Thatchtop and Hobrion Tel-Astra (Hobs) awoke after a good nights rest sleeping in the Dragonrest cloister. Harlen and Hobs slept in the Temple of Bahamut. Harlen deeply hoped for a "special" something from sleeping in the temple while Levi and Trenzor took rest in the in the carved out rooms by the great statue of Astalagan.

Runara was informed by Tarak that the group might be interested in helping the myconids that habited a cave on the south west corner of the island.

She reminded them to seek the advice of Tarak before heading out for the cave they were still interested in as he knew of potential routes of passage to the cave. In addition he supplied the group with much needed provisions to seek trade with the myconids if they could find their way into the caves.

The group was also greeted by Varnoth who spoke to them about mysterious ship crashes that kept taking place on the north eastern corner of the island by some dangerous reefs. The cause was unknown the people the cloister and warranted investigation.

Trenzor did the lions share of the rowing as the rest of the group was meet with a fair amount of sea sickness from rough waves going around the south western pass of the island.

They group were greeted by 3 fume drakes and fought on the intruders of the springs. The group quickly dispersed the fume drakes and Harlen provided cover from boat as the group explored the springs.

Trenzor called out his history with nature and unveiled the true origin of the springs as a great place of healing as it was a site of great bronze dragon that had perished fighting the evil dragons many years ago. The group all bathed in the magic spring and recovered from their new burns at the hand of the fume drakes. In the process they managed to harvest 6 of the magical wind spore mushrooms after Trenzor identified the mushrooms with some amazing nature rolls.

From there the group continued west to the cave entrance during high tide and attempted to swim in to the caves of the myconids. Much to their surprise they were greeted with a huge undead octupus that myconids had taken control of to serve as a guardian of the cave while they attempted to deal with a great blight that had fallen apon the colony. The group defeated the spore servant octopus with the help of Hobs as he twisted time and save Harlan from a nearly fatal pounding of the great creature.

From there the party meet the trepiditious myconids and introduced themselves as friends of Tarak. They were sent to barter and help them if they could. Upon arrival they were attacked by blighted mushrooms in the form of violet fungus that even the myconids were afraid of. They battled by the violet fungus and introduced to the myconids colony meeting Molen and Kraz.

From there they were take to meet their leader Sinensa, who was being tended to by Auranta and Enok. From there they were told of the great blight that was recking havoc on the myconids colony and the dire straights the colony was under and the need for a guardian.

The group decided to attempt to help the the myconids and investigate the source of the blight. They investigated the then dangerous cave and clear the cave of the remaining fume drakes. After Harlan snuck around the cave and proved it save the rest of the group followed and discovered the great crystal that was blocked the nature vents provided by the cave structure.

Hobs was able to learn of the crystals powers and it's link to a powerful fire plane up using some arcane intelligence that uncovered the source of the crystals power.

With the help of Levi's tool and Trenzor great strength they attempted to free the vents of the crystal by prying it out. They failed to hold the weight of the crystal but managed to free it only to have it crash and break on the floor unleashing their final adversary, a great fire snake. The group quickly took down the serpent at the cost of Trenzor who incured great blows after coming face to face with the great snake. Harlan's masterful use of his bow and shot and killed the great snake. The group found 25 shards of obsidian worth 10gp each.

The myconids rushed in to help after the source of the blight was purged from the cave system and attempted to shower the group in gifts and aid to help the recovery of Trenzor. The group need the session after a rest in what would normally by a very gross / slimy bed of the mushrooms but were soothed to sleep by the aid of the spore's that provided a soothing state to rest.

From here we continue the session next time....

10 Dec 2025

## 🤖 Claude

Here's a polished version for your Discord campaign chronicle:

SESSION 1: The Blight of Seagrow Caves

In which our heroes answer the call of friendship and delve into darkness

THE MORNING AT DRAGON'S REST

Our four adventurers—Trenzor (Druid of the Tall Trees), Harlen Vex (Fighter and Marksman), Levendel 'Levy' Thatchtop (Artificer and Tinkerer), and Hobrion Tel-Astra, called 'Hobs' (Wizard of Uncertain Time)—awoke refreshed after their first night as guests of the Dragon's Rest cloister.

Harlen and Hobs had chosen to sleep in the sacred Temple of Bahamut, with Harlen secretly hoping the Platinum Dragon might bestow some divine favor upon him in his dreams. Meanwhile, Levy and Trenzor rested in the carved chambers near the towering statue of Astalagan, the ancient bronze dragon whose legacy still watches over the sanctuary.

At dawn, they were warmly greeted by Runara, the young bronze dragon wyrmling who leads Dragon's Rest. She invited them to join the early-rising members of the cloister for breakfast, and extended an open invitation to return for the communal dinner served each evening after sundown.

It was Tarak the Flamesinger, the contemplative elf monk, who brought news of their first potential quest: the myconid colony inhabiting caves on the southwestern corner of Stormwreck Isle was in dire need of assistance. Tarak urged the party to seek his counsel before departing, as he knew the safest routes to reach the caves. True to his word, he provided them with valuable provisions—trade goods that might prove useful in negotiations with the fungal folk.

Varnoth, a concerned member of the cloister, also approached the party with troubling news: mysterious shipwrecks had been occurring with alarming frequency near the dangerous reefs on the island's northeastern shore. The cause remained unknown, and the matter warranted investigation when time allowed.

THE JOURNEY TO SEAGROW CAVES

After a hearty breakfast and detailed consultation with Tarak, the party decided on their approach: they would take a small boat along the southern coast of the island to reach the cave entrance during high tide.

The voyage proved more challenging than anticipated. While Trenzor bore the brunt of the rowing with druidic endurance, his companions found themselves battling waves of seasickness as the boat navigated the rough waters around the island's southwestern passage. It was not the most dignified beginning to their adventure, but they pressed on.

THE HOT SPRINGS & THE FUME DRAKES

Roughly halfway to their destination, the party spotted a clearing marked by steaming hot springs—exactly the location Tarak had mentioned might yield valuable herbs and mushrooms. They decided to make landfall and investigate.

Their arrival, however, was not welcomed. Three fume drakes—small, irritable creatures of smoke and flame—took exception to these intruders and attacked with fiery breath. The party quickly dispersed the territorial guardians, with Harlen providing expert cover fire from the boat while his companions explored the springs.

It was Trenzor, drawing upon his deep connection to nature, who unveiled the true significance of this sacred site. These were no ordinary hot springs—they were formed from the final resting place of a noble bronze dragon who had perished in ancient battle against the forces of chromatic evil. The waters still carried healing magic from that heroic sacrifice.

The party took the opportunity to bathe in the restorative springs, soothing their fresh burns from the fume drake encounter. During their rest, Trenzor's keen eye for flora identified six wind spore mushrooms growing nearby—rare specimens with valuable properties. His exceptional knowledge of nature (and some truly impressive die rolls) allowed them to harvest the mushrooms without damaging the delicate ecosystem.

THE SPORE SERVANT GUARDIAN

Refreshed and provisioned, the party continued westward, reaching the cave entrance at the optimal time: high tide, when the mouth of Seagrow Caves was accessible by water. They prepared to swim into the darkened cavern.

What they encountered was far from expected.

An enormous undead octopus—grotesque and covered in fungal growths—surged from the depths to confront them. The myconids, in their desperation to protect their ailing colony, had taken control of this "spore servant" to guard their home while they dealt with an internal crisis.

The battle was fierce. The undead creature's crushing tentacles nearly claimed Harlen's life in a devastating series of strikes. But in that crucial moment, Hobs bent the threads of time itself, reaching across causality to save his companion from what should have been a fatal pounding. With their combined efforts—and Hobs' timely intervention—the party defeated the guardian.

WELCOME TO THE MYCONID COLONY

Beyond the fallen guardian, the party encountered their first myconids: fungal folk who communicate through clouds of rapport spores. Though initially trepidatious, the myconids' fear eased when the adventurers introduced themselves as friends of Tarak, sent to barter and provide aid.

Their welcome was immediately tested. Blighted violet fungus—corrupted by the very plague afflicting the colony—attacked without warning. Even the myconids feared these twisted versions of what should have been harmless mushrooms. The party fought valiantly, clearing the infection, and properly introduced themselves to Molen and Kraz, who led them deeper into the colony.

At the heart of Seagrow Caves, they met the myconid sovereign Sinensa, who was being tended by her attendants Auranta and Enok. The sovereign was gravely ill, her telepathic voice weak as she explained the dire situation: a mysterious blight was destroying their colony from within, and their previous guardian—the octopus—had fallen to the corruption and risen as an undead abomination.

The colony was dying. They desperately needed help.

THE SOURCE OF THE BLIGHT

The party pledged their aid and began investigating the source of the corruption. Their search led them to a dangerously unstable section of the cave system, where the remaining fume drakes had made their nest.

Harlen volunteered to scout ahead, his fighter's instincts and steady nerves allowing him to navigate the treacherous passages. He confirmed the area was manageable, and the party followed, working together to clear out the hostile drakes.

At the far end of the cavern, they discovered the source of all their troubles: an enormous fire elemental crystal that had somehow lodged itself in the natural ventilation system of the caves. The crystal was blocking the airflow that kept the myconid colony healthy, and its planar heat was creating the conditions for blight to spread.

Hobs, drawing upon his arcane knowledge and keen intellect, examined the crystal carefully. His studies revealed its nature: a shard of the Elemental Plane of Fire, pulsing with barely-contained energy. It needed to be removed, but doing so would be extremely dangerous.

THE FIRE SNAKE

Levy produced his tools, and Trenzor lent his considerable strength to the effort. Together, they attempted to carefully pry the crystal free from where it had wedged itself into the rock. For a moment, it seemed they would succeed—

—and then the massive crystal's weight proved too much. It slipped from their grasp and crashed to the cavern floor, shattering into pieces.

From within the shattered crystal, wreathed in flame and fury, emerged their true final challenge: a fire snake, an elemental creature that had been trapped within the crystal's heart. The serpent of living flame struck with terrifying speed.

Trenzor, standing closest, bore the brunt of the creature's assault. Searing flames and crushing coils brought the druid perilously close to death. But the party rallied. Harlen, demonstrating the masterful archery that had served them so well throughout the day, loosed a perfectly-aimed arrow that struck the fire snake's vital core. The creature exploded in a shower of embers and went still.

The battle was won, but at great cost. Trenzor lay gravely wounded.

Among the shattered remains of the crystal, the party discovered 25 obsidian shards, each worth 10 gold pieces—a small fortune, and proof of their victory.

GRATITUDE OF THE MYCONIDS

The moment the fire snake fell, the temperature in the caves began to normalize. Fresh air flowed through the restored ventilation system. The blight's source had been purged.

The myconids rushed to the scene, their telepathic voices filled with overwhelming gratitude and relief. They immediately tended to Trenzor's wounds, and though the party had expected only simple thanks, the fungal folk showered them with gifts and healing aid.

That night, the party rested in what would normally have been rather unsettling sleeping arrangements—slimy, soft beds formed from the myconids' own fungal matter. But the myconids released soothing spores into the air, and the adventurers found themselves drifting into the most peaceful, restorative sleep they had experienced in weeks.

As consciousness faded, they could feel the gratitude of an entire colony flowing around them like a warm blanket. They had saved these gentle creatures from extinction.

They were heroes.

To be continued...

Next session: What awaits our heroes when they wake? And what of those mysterious shipwrecks in the northeast?

Notes for the DM:
Party successfully completed the Seagrow Caves quest
Trenzor's compass successfully guided them
Hobs' time manipulation ability introduced dramatically
Myconid colony saved, strong allies gained
Loot: 6 wind spore mushrooms, 25 obsidian shards (250 gp total)
Recommend Level Up to 2 before next session

THE MORNING AT DRAGON'S REST

Our four adventurers—Trenzor (Druid of the Tall Trees), Harlen Vex (Fighter and Marksman), Levendel 'Levy' Thatchtop (Artificer and Tinkerer), and Hobrion Tel-Astra, called 'Hobs' (Wizard of Uncertain Time)—awoke refreshed after their first night as guests of the Dragon's Rest cloister.

───────────────────────────────────────────────

THE HOT SPRINGS & THE FUME DRAKES

Roughly halfway to their destination, the party spotted a clearing marked by steaming hot springs—exactly the location Tarak had mentioned might yield valuable herbs and mushrooms.

Their arrival was not welcomed. Three fume drakes—small, irritable creatures of smoke and flame—took exception to these intruders and attacked with fiery breath. The party quickly dispersed the territorial guardians, with Harlen providing expert cover fire from the boat.

The party bathed in the restorative springs, soothing their fresh burns. During their rest, Trenzor's exceptional knowledge of nature allowed them to harvest six wind spore mushrooms—rare specimens with valuable properties.

───────────────────────────────────────────────

THE SPORE SERVANT GUARDIAN

Refreshed and provisioned, the party reached the cave entrance at high tide and prepared to swim into the darkened cavern.

An enormous undead octopus—grotesque and covered in fungal growths—surged from the depths to confront them. The myconids had taken control of this "spore servant" to guard their home while dealing with an internal crisis.

───────────────────────────────────────────────

Beyond the fallen guardian, the party encountered the myconids: fungal folk who communicate through clouds of rapport spores. Though initially fearful, they relaxed when the adventurers introduced themselves as friends of Tarak.

Blighted violet fungus—corrupted by plague—attacked without warning. The party fought valiantly, clearing the infection, and were introduced to Molen and Kraz, who led them deeper into the colony.

At the heart of Seagrow Caves, they met the myconid sovereign Sinensa, gravely ill and tended by Auranta and Enok. She explained the dire situation: a mysterious blight was destroying their colony from within. The colony was dying.

The party pledged their aid.

───────────────────────────────────────────────

THE SOURCE OF THE BLIGHT

Investigation led them to a dangerous section infested with fume drakes. Harlen scouted ahead, confirming the area was manageable, and the party cleared out the hostile creatures.

At the far end, they discovered the source: an enormous fire elemental crystal lodged in the natural ventilation system, blocking airflow and spreading corruption.

───────────────────────────────────────────────

THE FIRE SNAKE

Levy and Trenzor worked together to pry the crystal free. For a moment, success seemed certain—then the massive crystal slipped and crashed to the floor, shattering into pieces.

From within emerged a fire snake, wreathed in flame and fury.

Trenzor, standing closest, bore the brunt of the assault. Searing flames and crushing coils brought him perilously close to death. But Harlen, with masterful archery, loosed a perfectly-aimed arrow that struck the serpent's vital core.

Victory, but at great cost.

Among the shattered crystal: 25 obsidian shards worth 250 gold pieces.

───────────────────────────────────────────────

GRATITUDE OF THE MYCONIDS

With the fire snake defeated, fresh air flowed through the restored caves. The blight's source was purged.

The myconids rushed to help, showering the party with gratitude and healing aid. That night, the adventurers rested in fungal beds, lulled to sleep by soothing spores.

They had saved an entire colony from extinction.

They were heroes.

## 🤖 Claude

Smart foreshadowing! That's excellent DMing - planting the circus boat seed early so when they encounter the owlbear, it clicks into place rather than feeling random.

You could even have fun callbacks when they DO meet the owlbear:

Player sees owlbear with circus collar: "Wait... didn't Varnoth mention something about a circus ship?"

Trenzor's player, remembering: "The shipwrecks! One of them must have been carrying a menagerie!"

That moment of player realization is chef's kiss as a DM. They'll feel smart for connecting the dots, and you get to enjoy watching it click.

Fun Ideas for When They Encounter the Owlbear:

If they befriend it and bring it back to Dragon's Rest:

Runara: "Is that... oh my. Is that Barnaby? From Marvello's Menagerie? We heard they were shipwrecked months ago. The poor dear has been living wild all this time!"
Gives the owlbear a name and history
Maybe Runara tries to teach it new tricks

If they investigate the circus shipwreck later:

They find other clues: torn circus tents, broken cages, a ledger listing "Barnaby the Magnificent - Trained Owlbear"
Maybe other escaped animals are still out there (plot hooks!)
Could find the circus master's body with a journal describing the storm that wrecked them

Connecting to the time wizard:

Hobs might have a weird moment: "I remember this owlbear... but different. It was bigger? Angrier? Or was that a different loop?"
Adds to his temporal confusion

The recap is clean without it - saves the reveal for when it matters! Ready to plan what happens when they wake up in the myconid caves? 🍄

Sassy pirate + thief's guild character sheet backstory from the premade character sheet

## 🤖 Claude

Perfect! A sassy pirate halfling rogue with Thief's Guild connections - that's a fantastic character for this adventure, especially with all the shipwreck content on Stormwreck Isle!

That premade background usually includes:

Criminal/Pirate background with contacts in the underworld
Second-Story Work feature (climbing at full speed)
Fast Hands bonus action (Use Object, Sleight of Hand, thieves' tools)
Probably expertise in Stealth and Sleight of Hand
Great Story Hooks for Levy:

The Shipwrecks:

Does Levy recognize any of the wrecked ships from his pirating days?
"Wait... that's the Sea Serpent's Folly. I knew the captain. Bastard owed me money."
Maybe he's specifically here looking for rumored treasure from a particular wreck

The Circus Ship:

"Marvello's Menagerie? Oh, I've definitely heard of them. They passed through [port city]. Probably had valuables in their strongbox..."
Gives him personal motivation to investigate

Dragon's Rest Connections:

How does a pirate end up at a sanctuary?
Running from someone?
Heard rumors of treasure on the island?
Genuinely trying to go straight (but old habits die hard)?

Personality Moments:

Sassy comments when things go wrong
Eyeing valuables at Dragon's Rest (but not stealing from hosts... probably)
Sea shanties during the boat ride (before the seasickness hit)
"Why am I always the one crawling through tight spaces? Oh right, halfling."
Fun Session 1 Retroactive Moments:

During the boat ride:

Levy probably had opinions about Trenzor's rowing technique
"In my sailing days, we'd have made better time with half the effort. No offense, druid."

At the hot springs:

A pirate spotting treasure (the mushrooms): "Now those look valuable. Nice eye, Trenzor."

The fire crystal:

Classic rogue moment: "Let me get my tools. I've cracked tougher locks than this rock."

The obsidian shards:

Levy's eyes light up: "250 gold? Now we're talking. Split four ways... carry the one... not bad for a day's work!"

Want me to add some Levy-specific hooks or moments to your Notion guide for future sessions? His pirate background could tie into the shipwreck investigation beautifully!

## 👤 User

Ok - so tonight is chapter 2 - they all are going to wake up to a sedated dream state from - they are going to be in a brain fog as Sinensa is keeping them calm to sleep as she "listen's" to their dreams - then I think i have a perfect spot to try and tie in each character "explain their dream" and let them players explain their back story some as we all see the dream through their eyes of via the spores! - I do want to try and help build the tie in for the druid and is map charting in the caves too before they leave

23 Dec 2025

---

## 🤖 Claude

This is BRILLIANT! A shared dream sequence via myconid spores is such a perfect way to do backstory reveals in a natural, immersive way. Let me help you structure this:

SESSION 2 OPENING: The Dream Communion
Setting the Scene

When they wake (but not fully):

"As consciousness slowly returns, you find yourselves in a strange state - not quite asleep, not quite awake. The air is thick with luminescent spores that drift lazily through the chamber like stars. Your minds feel... connected. Shared. You can sense the presence of your companions, and something else - the ancient, gentle consciousness of Sinensa, the myconid sovereign, hovering at the edges of your thoughts.

Her telepathic voice is warm, apologetic: 'Forgive the intrusion, young ones. Your minds were troubled, wounded by fire and fear. I sought only to soothe... but in doing so, I have seen. Your stories. Your pasts. The paths that led you here.'

The dream-space shimmers, and suddenly you're all standing together in a place that isn't quite real - a void of soft light and drifting spores. Sinensa's presence pulses gently: 'You have shared much with each other in words. But dreams... dreams speak truths that words cannot. If you permit it, I would like to show you what I have seen. So you may know each other as I now know you.'

One by one, the dreams begin..."

Dream Sequence Structure
Order Suggestion:
Harlen Vex (Fighter) - Start with action/straightforward
Levy Thatchtop (Rogue) - Build into personality/sass
Hobs Tel-Astra (Wizard) - Get weird with time loops
Trenzor (Druid) - End emotionally with his tragedy and purpose

1. HARLEN'S DREAM

Prompt to Player: "Harlen, the dream-space shifts, and suddenly we're seeing through your eyes. What memory surfaces? What moment from your past defines who you are? Where are we, and what are you doing?"

DM Guidance After They Share:

Validate their story with sensory details
Have the other players "feel" Harlen's emotions through the spore connection
Sinensa comments: "Strength born of [their choice - duty/loss/determination]. You carry this with you still."

Transition: "The vision fades like morning mist, and the dream-space shifts again..."

2. LEVY'S DREAM

Prompt to Player: "Levy, the spores swirl, and now we're standing on a ship's deck - or perhaps a dock, or a shadowy alley. The smell of salt and tar fills the air. What do we see? What moment from your pirate days, your time with the guild, shaped the halfling you are today?"

DM Guidance After They Share:

Emphasize the sass/attitude even in the dream
Other players might "feel" Levy's cunning, his survival instincts
Sinensa: "Freedom and chains, both chosen. You run toward something, not just away."

Possible fun moment: If Levy's dream involves treasure/theft, have the dream-treasure turn into the obsidian shards they just found, connecting past to present

Transition: "The sea spray fades, and reality becomes... uncertain..."

3. HOBS' DREAM (This one should be WEIRD)

Prompt to Player: "Hobs, time fractures. The dream doesn't flow forward - it loops, it stutters, it shows multiple versions of the same moment happening at once. We see you reading the Looped Tome... or have we seen this before? Will we see it again? What moment trapped you in this curse? Or... which version of that moment do we see?"

DM Guidance After They Share:

Play up the temporal confusion
Have the dream repeat elements, stutter, or show alternate versions
The other players feel disoriented, experiencing a fraction of Hobs' curse
Sinensa sounds troubled: "Your time... is wounded. Folded upon itself. I see you reading the book, and reading it again, and it has not yet happened. This pain... I cannot fully comprehend."

Special touch:

After Hobs describes his moment with the Looped Tome, have the dream flicker
Show a flash of THIS moment (them sleeping in the myconid caves) from Hobs' perspective
"Wait... Hobs, you're seeing this NOW, aren't you? You've dreamed this before. You've BEEN here before. In another loop."
Let Hobs confirm he has vague memories of being in these caves in other timelines

Transition: "Time stabilizes - or perhaps it never was unstable. The confusion clears, and the dreams turn to older, deeper roots..."

4. TRENZOR'S DREAM (The Emotional Climax)

Prompt to Player: "Trenzor, the dream-space fills with the scent of parchment and ink, of maps and distant horizons. But there's smoke too. Fire. We're in a caravan, and something terrible is about to happen - or has just happened. Show us. Show us the moment that brought you to the Tall Trees. Show us your family."

DM Guidance After They Share:

This should be the most emotionally resonant
Have the other players SEE young Trenzor fleeing into the forest
Show the druids finding him
Show him learning to map the root networks and ley lines
End with his parents' compass pointing toward Stormwreck Isle
Sinensa, with deep empathy: "Loss. Growth. Purpose. You carry their legacy in every step, every map you draw. The island called to you because it knew: you are a mapmaker of balance, not just of land. You chart the paths between what was and what must be."

Connecting to the Caves: After Trenzor's dream, before they fully wake:

"Sinensa's presence pulses with understanding. 'Mapmaker's son... you seek to finish what they began. The caves you saved - they are part of the island's circulation, its breath. Would you... would you map them? So that others may know what you preserved?'

The dream-space shifts one final time, and you see the Seagrow Caves from above - a vast network of chambers and passages, like roots beneath a tree, like veins in a body. Sinensa shares her ancient knowledge of every tunnel, every chamber, every connection.

'This is my gift to you, Trenzor of the Tall Trees. Let your parents' work continue through you. Map what we could not.'"

WAKING UP - The Mapping Scene

When they fully wake:

"Your eyes flutter open. The spores have settled. You're lying in your fungal beds, but you all sit up at the same moment, looking at each other with new understanding. You've seen each other's souls.

Trenzor, on the stone beside your bed, you find materials: sheets of thin fungal parchment, a writing implement made from a hardened mushroom stalk filled with dark spore-ink, and a small satchel. Sinensa's telepathic voice whispers: 'For your map. And... thank you. For seeing us as worth saving.'"

Give Trenzor a moment:

Let him describe starting the map
The myconids help, showing him the full extent of the caves
He can add it to his parents' partial map of Stormwreck Isle
This is a beautiful character moment

While Trenzor maps, the others:

Discuss what they saw in each other's dreams
RP their reactions to the backstories
Prepare to leave
Benefits of This Scene

Narrative:

Backstory reveals without awkward "let me tell you about my past" exposition
Builds party bonds through shared vulnerability
Gives each player a spotlight moment
Establishes the myconids as deeply empathetic allies

Mechanical:

Trenzor gets a map of Seagrow Caves (useful if they need to return)
Party has detailed knowledge of the cave system
Could give them advantage on future Navigation checks around the island (Trenzor's maps are comprehensive now)

Thematic:

Reinforces the "balance and connection" themes
Shows myconid culture (dream-sharing is intimate for them)
Makes the party feel like true heroes whose stories matter
Transition to Next Quest

After the mapping is done and they're preparing to leave:

Sinensa: "You have given us life. If ever you need sanctuary, these caves are yours. But I sense... your work on this island is not finished. There are other wounds. Other imbalances. The dragon-child, Runara - she will have need of you. And perhaps... you will find more of your parents' trail, Trenzor."

The myconids see them off:

Gifts of goodberries (they grow them as thanks)
Maybe a Spore Servant Crab companion for one encounter as an escort
Molen and Kraz offer to guide them back to the coast

When they emerge from the caves:

It's late morning/early afternoon
They can return to Dragon's Rest or investigate the shipwrecks
Trenzor's compass might react to something...
Pro Tips for Running This

Pacing:

Give each dream 5-10 minutes
Don't rush them - this is important character development
If a player struggles, ask guiding questions:
"What do you see?"
"Who else is there?"
"What are you feeling in this moment?"

Player Agency:

Some players LOVE this, others might be shy
If someone's uncomfortable, Sinensa can say: "This memory is too private. I withdraw." and move on
Let them control how much they reveal

Sinensa's Role:

She's a gentle guide, not intrusive
She comments on themes, not specifics
She apologizes for the intrusion but wanted to help them heal

The Spore Connection:

Other players can "feel" emotions but don't control the dream
They're witnesses, not participants
Creates empathy without stealing spotlight

This should be a powerful opening to Session 2! Want me to help plan what happens when they return to Dragon's Rest or head to investigate the shipwrecks?
